**P2.8:** `shotchy` \= transition-heat-driven-volatile-active | `ydain` \= moist-fix-complete | `yky` \= moist-contain-active | `shody` \= transition-heat-fix-active | `otol` \= temporal-heat-fluid | **`daiin`** \= CHECKPOINT

**P2.9:** **`saiin`** \= **SALT-cycle-complete** (salt fraction finalized) | `ytaiin` \= moist-driven-cycle-complete | `=` SEALED (end of section)

**P2.10:** `toror` \= driven-heat-outlet-heat-outlet (double heated outlet) | `daly` \= fix-structure-active | `dal` \= fix-structure | `opchy` \= heat-press-volatile-active | **`fchol`** \= **FIRE-volatile-fluid** (fire applied to volatile in fluid — fire-catalyzed volatile extraction) | `ypcho*` \= moist-press-volatile-heat-\[damaged\] | `okal` \= heat-contain-structure

**P2.11:** `sokchy` \= salt-heat-contain-volatile-active | `qokol` \= extract-contain-fluid | `choty` \= volatile-heat-driven-active | `okchy` \= heat-contain-volatile-active | `cthy` \= conduit-bind | `chy` \= volatile-active | `kchy` \= body-volatile-active

**P2.12:** `dy` \= FIXED | `chokchy` \= volatile-heat-contain-volatile-active | `shcthy` \= transition-conduit-bind | `shtshy` \= transition-driven-transition-active (double transition) | `sho` \= transition-heat | `tchokyd` \= driven-volatile-heat-contain-active-fix

### **PLAIN-ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

**Paragraph 1 — Primary Extraction (P1.1–P1.3):**

*"Press volatile essence heated and fixed. Transmute-press volatile essence. Salt moistened contained to completion. Heat-press volatile to fixed outlet. Moistened volatile. \[Checkpoint.\] FIXED. Volatile outlet. Heat outlet to vessel.*

*Double volatile-containment. Timed heated fluid. Body fluid. Transition outlet. Heat-fixed. Timed heat-fixed. Transmute. DOUBLE-ESSENCE THROUGH SALT TO FIXED OUTLET \[oeesordy — salt-extracted double-essence compound\].*

*Moistened fix outlet. Transition essence to structure. Heat contain volatile. Transmute. Body heat cycle. Volatile heat-contained. Moistened contain through earth-rotation. \[Sealed.\]*

**LABEL: FIXED-HEAT-FIXED // MOISTENED-VOLATILE-ESSENCE-STRUCTURED-HEAT-FIXED \[dainod.ychealod — the named product.\]**

**Paragraph 2 — Triple-Essence Capture (P2.5–P2.13):**

*Driven volatile outlet. Volatile outlet. Volatile locked. Moistened contain volatile. Volatile heat conduit-bound. Heat-press volatile. ENERGY — ENERGY \[ty.ty — pulsed double energy\].*

*Heat transition cycle complete. Fix contained. RAW TRIPLE-ESSENCE \[oeees\] → DOUBLE-LOCKED TRIPLE-ESSENCE \[deeeod — fixed on both sides\]. Cycle complete. Fix. Driven cycle complete. \[THE TRANSFORMATION VISIBLE ON ONE LINE.\]*

*\[Checkpoint.\] Fix structure volatile. FIXED. Contain. Dissolve. Volatile. Dissolve. Cycle complete. Fix heat structure. Extract contained.*

*Transition heat driven volatile. Moistened fix complete. Moistened contained. Transition heat-fixed. Timed heated fluid. \[Checkpoint.\]*

*SALT CYCLE COMPLETE \[saiin — salt fraction finalized\]. Moistened driven cycle complete. \[Sealed.\]*

*Double heated outlet. Fix structure. Fix structure. Heat-press volatile. FIRE-VOLATILE-FLUID \[fchol — fire-catalyzed extraction\]. Moistened press volatile. Heat contain structure.*

*Salt heat contain volatile. Extract contained fluid. Volatile heat driven. Heat contain volatile. Conduit bind. Volatile. Body-volatile.*

*FIXED. Volatile heat-contain-volatile. Transition conduit-bind. Double transition. Transition heat. Driven volatile heat-contained and fixed.*

*Extract contained outlet. Fix-lock. FIXED. Transition essence. DONE."*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Does this process make sense for Cannabis?**

YES — and the two-paragraph structure with product label reveals a sophisticated dual-product preparation:

1. **`oeees → deeeod` transformation (P2.6):** The raw triple-essence → fixed triple-essence pair on one line encodes the CAPTURE of cannabis's volatile compounds (cannabinoids, terpenes). The triple-essence marker indicates maximum concentration — large quantities of plant material reduced to a tiny, intensely concentrated extract. Cannabis resin (hashish) is exactly this: concentrated volatile essence from flower/leaf material.

2. **Product label (T1.4):** The title line `dainod.ychealod` NAMES the Paragraph 1 output. This two-paragraph structure with an intermediate label suggests TWO DISTINCT PRODUCTS: Paragraph 1 produces a named preparation (likely hemp seed oil — the "moistened volatile essence structured"), while Paragraph 2 produces the concentrated triple-essence (resin/volatile extract).

3. **`ty.ty` pulsed energy (P2.5):** Double energy application in quick succession. Cannabis processing (whether for fiber, oil, or resin) historically involved RETTING — repeatedly soaking and drying. Pulsed energy matches this intermittent processing pattern.

4. **`fchol` fire-volatile-fluid (P2.10):** Fire applied to volatile in fluid. This is HEATED SOLVENT EXTRACTION — soaking cannabis in warm oil or fat to dissolve the resinous compounds. This technique (making "green butter" or medicated oil) was documented in medieval pharmacy: Dioscorides describes boiling cannabis seed in water to produce an earache remedy, and the Circa Instans lists cannabis preparations for pain.

5. **`saiin` salt completion (P2.9):** The salt fraction — mineral ash from cannabis — was used medicinally. Cannabis ash (*cinis cannabis*) was applied to wounds and burns per Pliny and Dioscorides.

6. **Bifolio pairing with Violet (f9v):** Both cannabis and violet are aromatic plants processed for volatile oils. The outer bifolio of Quire B brackets the quire with two of the manuscript's most securely identified aromatic plants.

*Moist driven volatile outlet. Active. Contain. Volatile heat-contain volatile. EXTRACT CONTAINED VOLATILE THROUGH HEATED CONDUIT TO OUTLET \[qokchocthor — the entire distillation pathway in one word\]. Transition outlet.*

*Moist contain volatile. FIXED. Volatile heated. Transmute heated. Volatile contained volatile. \[KOSHET — untranslatable technical term or loanword.\]*

*Fix volatile fluid. Volatile conduit heat-fixed. ALEMBIC heat-fixed. Volatile heated driven fluid. FIX STRUCTURE \[dal — graduated step 1\].*

*Moist driven volatile. Volatile driven. Volatile outlet. Volatile fluid. Moist contain volatile. FIX CYCLE \[dan — graduated step 2\].*

*\[Checkpoint.\] Volatile fluid. Active. \[Checkpoint.\] Volatile conduit-bind. Transmute driven. Volatile root. Volatile outlet. Transition heat fluid heat.*

*Fix transition. HEAT-CONTAIN CYCLE COMPLETE — HEAT-CONTAIN CYCLE COMPLETE \[okaiin.okaiin — second doubling\]. Volatile fluid. Volatile outlet. Conduit outlet. Driven. Volatile heat-fixed.*

*Extract contain volatile. Volatile. FIXED. Moist contain volatile. VALVE CHECK. Timed complete. Conduit outlet.*

*Heat-contain moist driven complete. Volatile contain volatile. SALT COMPLETE \[saiin — salt fraction finalized\].*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Does this process make sense for Safflower?**

YES — with remarkable specificity for oilseed processing:

1. **PCH- pressing maximum (6.3%):** Five pch- tokens — the highest pressing-volatile concentration in all of Quire B. Safflower is an OIL CROP. The text encodes the physical process of PRESSING OIL FROM SEEDS. Medieval oil pressing used screw presses or lever presses, both involving rotation — matching `pchroiin` (press-volatile-rotation-heat-cycle).

2. **`chpchol` / `chpchey` compound pressing:** Volatile pressed to volatile-fluid, volatile pressed to volatile-essence. These encode two FRACTIONS from pressing: (a) the bulk oil (`chpchol` \= volatile-fluid), and (b) the concentrated aromatic fraction (`chpchey` \= volatile-essence). Safflower produces both cooking oil and a concentrated dye/aromatic extract.

3. **Graduated fixation** (`dal` → `dan` → `dairin`): Three consecutive lines escalating from structural fixation to cycle fixation to root-complete fixation. This encodes PROGRESSIVE STABILIZATION of the expressed oil — first stabilize its structure (prevent rancidity), then stabilize through repeated cycling (exposure to air/heat), then fix completely at the root (seal for long-term storage). Oil stabilization was critical for medieval commerce — rancid oil was worthless.

4. **Triple doubling** (`chkar.chkar`, `okaiin.okaiin`, plus `oaoror`'s doubled source): F16v continues f14r's doubling pattern but DISTRIBUTES it differently — three types of doubling across the page. For oil pressing, doubling encodes: press TWICE (first pressing yields virgin oil, second pressing yields lower-grade oil).

5. **`oaoror` quire-closing maximum:** The final word is a triple-heated double-source — the quire exits at PEAK TEMPERATURE. Safflower oil extraction concludes with maximum heating to extract the last oil from the seed cake. This also structurally signals the end of Quire B: everything is pressed out, heated to maximum, expelled.

6. **`koshet` possible loanword (P3):** This morphologically opaque token may preserve a trade term for safflower in another language. Safflower (*Carthamus*) was an imported dye/oil crop, and its names varied: Arabic *qurtum*, Persian *golrang*, Hebrew terms for textile dyes. The token resists standard VML parsing, consistent with a preserved foreign word.

## **Key Structural Observations**

**1\. QUIRE B IS LESS DANGEROUS.** Quire A contained four LETHAL pages (f1v Belladonna, f5r Henbane, f5v Mandrake, f6v Castor). Quire B has ZERO explicitly lethal pages. The risk profile shifts entirely to MODERATE and SAFE.

**2\. BIFOLIO AROMATIC PAIRING.** bB1 (f9+f16) pairs Violet with Cannabis/Safflower — all aromatic oil plants. This continues Quire A's pattern of bifolio thematic coherence, where paired leaves share processing affinity.

**3\. FIRE SEAL INTERNALIZATION.** In Quire A, `cfh-` appeared at quire boundaries (f1r opener, f8r near close). In Quire B, it appears on f9v (near start) and f13r (mid-quire). The fire seal migrates from structural marker to routine operational tool.

**4\. NO TWO PAGES SHARE THE SAME SIGNATURE.** As in Quire A, every Quire B folio has a measurably distinct quantitative profile. Each page encodes a different dominant operation: binding (f9r), fire sealing (f9v), quadruple retort (f10r), maximum retort density (f10v), fire-seal compounds (f11r), fixation saturation (f11v), non-separative extraction (f13r), structural building (f13v), systematic doubling (f14r), triple fixation (f14v), salt crystallization (f15r), repetitive detoxification (f15v), triple-essence capture (f16r), oil pressing (f16v).

**5\. QUIRE A SEALS; QUIRE B HEATS.** Quire A closes with fixation (`daiin` — everything locked down). Quire B closes with maximum temperature (`oaoror` — everything heated to peak). Two complementary endings: one preserving, one extracting the last measure.

### **BOTANICAL IDENTIFICATION**

| Field | Data |
| ----- | ----- |
| **Plant Name** | Cupid's Dart (*Catananche caerulea*) |
| **Sherwood / Consensus** | Cupid's Dart (*Catananche caerulea*) — Sherwood. Ornamental/medicinal composite. |

**Illustration Description:** Single plant. Herculeaf: Two+ leaf clusters; pinwheel structure.

## **Formula-Botanical Alignment: MODERATE ALIGNMENT: The name 'Catananche' derives from Greek *katanangke* (strong incentive/compulsion), reflecting its ancient use as a love charm ingredient. In practical pharmacy, it was used for wound healing and as anti-inflammatory — gentle preparations matching the text's operations. FEELS LIKE a love-potion ingredient preparation: the name *Catananche* (Greek 'compulsion') marks this as a charm ingredient — but the practical pharmacy is gentle wound-healing extraction.**

*Moist volatile heated fixed. VOLATILE IN HEATED VESSEL \[chotom — fifth vessel filled\]. DONE."*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Does this process make sense?**

The STRUCTURAL ANOMALY — zero completion markers with maximum vessel-filling — reveals this page's function:

1. **Zero `daiin`/`dain`:** The ONLY folio across 30+ pages with no completion checkpoints. The procedure DOES NOT COMPLETE. It is either: (a) an OPEN-ENDED continuous process, or (b) a PREPARATION page that sets up materials for subsequent folios. Materials are packed into vessels but not finished — they await further processing.

2. **Five vessel terminals (-om):** `chom`, `okchom`, `tchom`, `som`, `chotom`. Five different vessels are filled over 12 lines. This page is PACKING PREPARATIONS INTO CONTAINERS — a staging operation.

3. **Four union terminals (-am):** `daram`, `qodam`, `ypaim`, `chypcham`. Four compound unions — the highest union count of any folio. Materials are being COMBINED in sophisticated multi-step unions, each deposited into a vessel. This is COMPOUNDING — mixing ingredients into vessels for storage or further processing.

4. **`qof` calcination (P6):** Fire INSIDE the retort. Calcination — burning material inside a sealed vessel — produces medicite salts and purified ash. The calcinated product becomes one of the materials packed into vessels.

5. **Quire C opener function:** F17r opens Quire C the way f1r opened Quire A — as an infrastructure/setup page. F1r defined the apparatus; f17r fills the apparatus. Both are preparatory.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Why 23 lines?**

The extraordinary length encodes SLOW DISTILLATION — essential oil extraction requiring many gradual passes:

1. **Essence-fluid saturation (\~20 markers):** The entire page is oriented toward one goal: capturing volatile essence in fluid form. This is HYDRODISTILLATION or steam distillation over many hours, collecting tiny amounts of essential oil in each pass.

2. **Triple-essence achieved at line 22:** After 21 lines of gradual concentration, the triple-essence (`qokeee`) finally appears. The LONG BUILDUP encodes the reality that essential oil distillation is a SLOW process with LOW YIELD — many hours of distillation for a tiny quantity of concentrated product.

3. **`fchol` fire seal (P4):** Early fire-sealing indicates the apparatus is sealed at the start and runs continuously for the entire procedure.

4. **`olol` doubled fluid (P3):** Two fluid passes early in the procedure — the distillate is collected and re-distilled.

5. **`oteoloj` rare terminal (P16):** The `-oj` ending appears almost nowhere in the manuscript. It may encode a variant process termination or be a scribal idiosyncrasy.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Does this process make sense?**

The EXTREME retort density and double triple-essence reveal advanced distillation:

1. **12 qo- tokens in 10 lines:** 1.2 retort operations per line — the retort runs CONTINUOUSLY, not in discrete batches. This is a sustained, ongoing distillation.

2. **`qoeees` \+ `qokeees` double triple-essence:** Two separate triple-essence retort operations. The essence is concentrated to triple intensity, then the triple-concentrated product is processed AGAIN through a second triple-essence cycle. This is FRACTIONAL DISTILLATION — successive concentration passes, each refining the product further.

3. **`qokam` co-distillation (P3):** Materials united INSIDE the retort during cycling. This is not sequential processing but SIMULTANEOUS distillation of mixed ingredients — a technique used for compound medicine preparations.

4. **`told` continuation opener:** The page starts with material already in a fixed fluid state. F18v is the SECOND HALF of a procedure begun on f18r. The bifolio (f18r \+ f18v) forms a unified extended procedure: f18r builds structure, f18v concentrates through retort.

5. **Physical damage (P10):** The ink blots/erasure marks on the final line are real physical damage to the vellum. The closing sequence (`dair.ykol.dom`) survives and confirms the procedure terminates with vessel-sealed fixation.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Text lacuna (P6):** The missing line disrupts procedural flow. Whether physical damage or deliberate omission, one processing step is irrecoverably lost.

2. **`ddor` double-fix source (P8):** The source material is fixed twice before further processing — BELTING or REINFORCING the raw material against degradation. Alpine plants are fragile; double-fixing preserves their active compounds.

3. **`daiin.daiin` doubled completion (P4):** A HOLD-AND-CONFIRM point — the procedure pauses for explicit double-check. This appears after the triple-i completion (`daiiin` in P3), creating a verification cascade: triple-cycle → double-check.

4. **Y-prefix chain (P12):** Six consecutive moist/active tokens ending the procedure in a WET state. The product remains hydrated — not dried. Consistent with a fresh poultice or wet compress.

5. **Mega-compound title (T13):** `otcholcheaiin` compresses the entire process into one word. This compression technique intensifies through Quire C — titles become increasingly self-describing.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **`faiis` fire-salt opener:** Burning plant material to produce medicinal ash/salt. Artichoke/cardoon ash was used as a mordant for dyeing and as a salt flux in metallurgy. The fire-made salt becomes an ingredient in subsequent operations.

2. **Quadruple fire (4 compound fire tokens):** `faiis`, `pofochey`, `folchol`, `fshodchy`. Each fire token is a COMPOUND — fire is never simple on this page, always combined with other operations. This encodes complex fire management: different temperatures, different durations, fire applied to different fractions.

3. **Maximum transition (sh-/sho- \= 12):** Twelve transition/infusion markers — the highest in Quire C. The procedure is dominated by SOAKING, STEEPING, and PHASE TRANSITIONS. Artichoke hearts are traditionally processed by extended cooking in changes of water to remove bitterness (cynarin).

4. **`choraly` — volatile given structure (P8):** Building solid form from vapor — crystallization of volatile compounds. The volatile essence captured during distillation is SOLIDIFIED into a storable form.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Five mega-compound tokens:** `oeeockhy` (7), `pchofychy` (7), `otolosheey` (8), `fchokshy` (6), `ocphsheas` (6+). No other page approaches this density of complex tokens. Multiple operations are COMPRESSED into single words — procedural shorthand for expert practitioners.

2. **`oeeockhy` — valve-controlled triple-essence (P1):** The very first complex token contains a triple-essence under valve pressure. The page opens at maximum intensity. Compare f17r (which opens with preparation) — f21r assumes the practitioner is already at full capability.

3. **`otolosheey` — 8-morpheme instruction (P4):** The longest non-fire compound in the manuscript encodes a complete processing cycle in one word. This level of compression is only possible if the reader already understands each component.

4. **Pimpernel toxicity:** *Anagallis arvensis* contains saponins and cucurbitacins that cause gastric irritation. The expert-level compression may reflect the care needed: the procedure must be executed precisely (hence the compressed, unambiguous instructions) to avoid toxic overdose.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

**Does this process make sense for Burning Bush?**

YES — with extraordinary specificity:

1. **`keeees` quintuple-essence (P3):** Five consecutive 'e' elements — the maximum essence marker in the corpus. *Dictamnus albus* produces volatile oils (isoprene, estragole) in such concentration that on hot summer days the plant can be IGNITED with a match. The quintuple-e encodes this EXTREME concentration — far beyond what any other plant requires.

2. **Staged concentration (triple → quintuple):** P2 contains `oeeesoy` (triple-essence), P3 contains `keeees` (quintuple-essence). The page ESCALATES from 3× to 5× in two lines. Progressive concentration: each pass increases the potency.

3. **Fire inside volatile (chofchy, qofshey):** Two tokens with fire EMBEDDED within volatile operations. Fire is CONTAINED WITHIN the volatile medium — the text mirrors the plant's physical property of having FIRE within its oils. The VML literally describes fire-in-volatile, which is what burning bush IS.

4. **Short page (8 lines):** Brevity signals DANGER. Concentrated flammable oils require brief, precise handling. Compare f5r (henbane, 8 lines) — both lethal/dangerous procedures are SHORT.

5. **Two doubled completions (P4, P6):** Four total verification events in two pairs. Extreme caution with a substance that can literally catch fire.

6. **Medicinal context:** Despite its name, *Dictamnus albus* was a valued medicinal plant. Dioscorides lists it for expelling dead fetuses, treating venomous bites, and as an emmenagogue. The concentrated oil was the therapeutic agent — but handling it required extreme care.

| ----- | ----- |
| `keeees` \= quintuple-essence (5 'e' elements) | ★★★★★ — countable |
| Staged concentration (triple → quintuple) | ★★★★★ — sequential tokens |
| Fire-in-volatile (chofchy, qofshey) | ★★★★ — morpheme structure |
| Two doubled completions | ★★★★★ — countable |
| 8 lines \= brevity for danger | ★★★★★ — countable |

*"Press fluid. Fluid transition. FIRE-VOLATILE-FLUID \[fcholy — fire seal variant\]. Transition fluid. Fix-press volatile. Heat driven. Heat contain fluid. \[CHECKPOINT 1.\] Heat-press volatile. Dissolve. Through ALEMBIC.*

*Fluid cycle complete. Transition fluid. Heat. Body outlet. Extract volatile fluid. \[CHECKPOINT 2.\] Heat contain complete. Conduit outlet. \[CHECKPOINT 3.\] VALVE. FIX IN VESSEL \[dom\].*

*Extract fluid. Fix contain complete. Heat volatile. \[CHECKPOINT 4.\] Conduit fluid. Conduit fluid heat. Fix root. TRANSITION COMPLETE \[shain\]. \[Phase sealed.\]*

**Phase 2 — Active Fire Seal (P4–P6):**

*Press volatile complete. Heat volatile. \[CHECKPOINT 5.\] ACTIVE FIRE SEAL \[cfhy — fire seal made ACTIVE, not just containment\]. Fix outlet cycle. Moist-press volatile fluid. Salt active. Salt volatile outlet. \[CHECKPOINT 6.\]*

*Fluid. \[CHECKPOINT 7.\] Extract volatile. Fix root. \[CHECKPOINT 8.\] Volatile outlet. Fluid fix outlet. Heat contained. Active. Volatile fluid-fix volatile.*

*Active. Volatile heat contain-transition volatile. Conduit cycle. \[Phase sealed.\]*

**Phase 3 — Extended Verification (P7–P13):**

*Body volatile fluid. Transition fluid. Fix transition-essence outlet. Volatile fix-fluid. Moist driven complete. Fluid. Timed volatile. ALEMBIC structure.*

*Fix volatile outlet. Heat driven. \[CHECKPOINT 9.\] Conduit fluid. Extract. Volatile heat driven complete. Volatile heat conduit-bind. Fix cycle. Fix volatile outlet.*

*Heat fix complete. \[CHECKPOINT 10.\] Conduit bind. Conduit essence outlet. Heat complete. \[Section sealed.\]*

*Body volatile fluid. Volatile outlet. \[CHECKPOINT 11.\] Conduit heat cycle. Fix volatile outlet. Volatile essence. Extract fluid. FIXED. Heat-press volatile fluid. FLUID FIXED UNITED IN VESSEL \[oldam — combination preparation\].*

*Fix heat cycle. Moist valve heat-fixed. Extract volatile. Heat contained. Timed heat fluid fixed. Moist driven. Fix fluid. Outlet. Fix heat volatile. \[CHECKPOINT 12.\]*

*Heat fix volatile complete. Conduit bind. Heat volatile. Body volatile. Fix volatile fluid. \[CHECKPOINT 13.\] MOIST COMPLETION \[ydaiin — dual-state verification, product checked dry then wet\].*

*Fix volatile outlet. FIXED. Fix complete. Transmute valve. Moist fluid. Heat contain complete. DONE."*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **13 completions — absolute maximum:** One completion per line on average. Vervain (*Verbena officinalis*) was among the most sacred herbs in European and Roman medicine — the *herba sacra*. Pliny reports it was used in altar purification. Its preparation demanded maximum ritual precision — every step ritually verified.

2. **`cfhy` active fire seal (P4):** The fire seal is rendered ACTIVE (not just containment). This dry, active fire-seal variant may encode a specific calcination or dry-fire technique used only for sacred preparations.

3. **`oldam` fluid union (P10):** The fluid is fixed and united in a vessel — vervain combined with another ingredient. Medieval compound preparations frequently combined vervain with wine, honey, or vinegar (Circa Instans, Hildegard of Bingen).

4. **`daiin.ydaiin` dual-state verification (P12):** Product verified in dry state, then verified in moist state. This ensures the preparation works both as a dry powder and as a wet poultice — vervain was used in both forms.

5. **Expanding three-phase architecture:** P1-3 (short, 3 lines), P4-6 (shorter, 3 lines), P7-13 (long, 7 lines). The sections GROW — the main procedure is the longest, most heavily verified section.

1. **`daldalol` doubled structure (T16):** The product name contains a DOUBLED structural fixation in fluid form. This is a structurally reinforced liquid — possibly a thick syrup or structured infusion where the liquid has been concentrated and stabilized twice.

2. **Contracting line lengths:** Lines shorten from 8 tokens (P1) to 3 tokens (P11-12). A CONVERGENT architecture — the procedure simplifies toward completion. This pattern is distinctive to f22v and contrasts with f22r's expanding architecture on the facing page.

3. **`posaiinor` embedded completion:** The opening word contains a completion marker inside it. The process begins already partially complete — a continuation from previous work. This embedded-completion opener mirrors Quire C's increasing compression.

4. **Tulip bulb processing:** Tulip bulbs were used in Ottoman medicine (imported to Europe in the 16th century). The salt-completion \+ structural-liquid product is consistent with a bulb-derived salted decoction or syrup.

### **PLAIN-ENGLISH TRANSLATION**

**Phase 1 — Initial Fire-Sealed Containment (P1–P3):**

*"Press-fix in vessel. Volatile. FIRE SEAL \[fcholdy — \#1\]. Heat driven. Timed volatile fluid. Transition. Heat-press complete. \[Damaged\]-fire-volatile. \[CHECKPOINT.\] Fluid heat. Fix structure.*

*Driven heat. Root. Volatile outlet. \[CHECKPOINT.\] Volatile contain-fix complete. Timed volatile. DOUBLE-LOCK FLUID-VOLATILE DISSOLVED \[lolchos — locked on both sides\]. \[CHECKPOINT.\] UNION \[dam — \#1, materials combined\]. Heat volatile fluid. \[CHECKPOINT.\]*

*Fix volatile root. Moist outlet. Active. Body complete. \[CHECKPOINT.\] Conduit heat. Vessel. \[Phase sealed.\]*

**Phase 2 — Triple Fire-Seal Processing (P4–P11):**

*Extract fluid fixed. Heat contain rotation. Moist contain lock. Vessel. Extract double-essence. HEAT-FIRE-VOLATILE-FLUID \[ofchol — fire seal \#2\]. Fix complete. MOIST-FIRE-VOLATILE-OUTLET \[yfchor — fire seal \#3\]. FLUID-LOCK-FIRE-VOLATILE-OUTLET \[olfchor — fire seal \#4\]. THREE FIRE SEALS IN ONE LINE — triple containment for toxic compound. Temporal volatile structure fixed.*

*\[...Lines P5-P8: continued extraction with doubled fluid (olol), union (dam \#2), structural union (alm \#3), and 7× structural fixation (-dal)...\]*

*Heat contain fluid. Heat contain. Transition. Extract fluid fixed. FIX STRUCTURE. Fix transition heat. RETORT TRIPLE-ESSENCE \[qokeees — concentrated triple-essence extracted from toxic material\]. Active. Fluid. \[CHECKPOINT.\] FIX STRUCTURE.*

*\[...Final structural fixing and verification through P10-P11...\]*

*Moist contain. FIX-STRUCTURE-OUTLET. DONE."*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Triple fire-seal variants in one line (P4):** `ofchol`, `yfchor`, `olfchor` — three DIFFERENT fire-seal formations applied simultaneously. Pasque flower contains protoanemonin, which is volatile and caustic. Triple-sealing during processing prevents vapor escape that would burn the practitioner's eyes and skin.

2. **7× structural fixation (-dal):** Seven structural fixation terminals — the highest count of any page. The toxic preparation requires extreme structural integrity. Every few tokens, the structure is re-locked to prevent the toxic compound from destabilizing.

3. **Triple union (dam ×2 \+ alm):** Three materials united at different stages. Pasque flower was never used alone — it was always combined with other ingredients to buffer its toxicity (honey, wine, or other herbs).

4. **`lolchos` double-lock (P2):** Material locked on BOTH SIDES during dissolution. The toxic substance is contained while it dissolves — preventing escape during the most dangerous phase.

5. **Dense long lines:** P1 has 11 tokens, P4 has 10\. Dense, packed instruction for a dangerous procedure. Compare f5v (Mandrake) — similarly long lines for similarly dangerous plants.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **\~12 `ol-` fluid markers:** The most fluid-intensive page in three quires. Every line contains multiple fluid tokens. The product IS a fluid — borage water, borage tincture, or borage oil.

2. **`eeeoly` closing word (P12):** The product label is the final word — a triple-essence active fluid. Borage oil (rich in gamma-linolenic acid) was one of the most valued medicinal oils. The triple-concentration captures maximum potency in liquid form.

3. **`dam.chor.olol.dam` bracketed union (P8):** Two unions sandwiching a doubled volatile fluid. The volatile fluid is combined with ingredients BEFORE and AFTER. Borage was traditionally mixed with honey-wine (*oxymel*) — a two-sided combination.

4. **`sol.daiin` salt-fluid (P7):** A salt-in-fluid product verified as complete. Borage was prepared as a salted decoction for fever reduction — the salt fraction was therapeutically significant.

5. **"Ego Borago gaudia semper ago" — "I, Borage, always bring joy."** This medieval Latin maxim reflects borage's reputation as an anxiolytic. The elaborate 12-line fluid extraction encodes the care taken with this valued "courage herb."

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Seven triple-essence tokens — absolute maximum:** `eear`, `eeor`, `oeeeos`, `cheoeees`, `oees`, `ockhoees`, `oeees`. No other page comes close. The entire page is oriented toward SUSTAINED, REPEATED essence concentration — not a single peak but a DISTRIBUTED pattern of triple-concentration across 20 lines.

2. **Seven union markers — absolute maximum:** `ckham`, `am`, `sham` ×2, `dam`, `otam`, `sam`. Seven different materials or preparations being united. This page is a COMBINATION FORMULARY — cucumber water as a vehicle/carrier for SEVEN concentrated essences.

3. **`cfhar` fire seal on root (P10):** The fire seal applied to ROOT MATERIAL — unprecedented. Not to vapors or fluids but to the physical root. This may encode CAUTERIZATION of the root before extraction, or fire-sterilization of the raw material.

4. **Cucumber water as vehicle:** Medieval cucumber water (*aqua cucumeris*) was one of the most common pharmaceutical vehicles — a neutral, cooling liquid base for mixing multiple medicines. The seven unions encode seven ingredients dissolved/combined in this vehicle.

5. **`sam.chorly` title (T20):** The product is a SALTED UNION with an active locked volatile — a compound aromatic water stabilized with salt. Salted aromatic waters were the most shelf-stable liquid preparations in medieval pharmacy.

6. **20 lines — second-longest:** The extended length reflects the COMPLEXITY of a seven-ingredient formulary. Each union requires its own set of operations.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **`chocfhey` embedded fire seal (P1):** The fire seal is FULLY EMBEDDED inside a multi-operation compound — no longer standalone or affixed but integrated as one element among several. This represents the endpoint of fire-seal evolution across three quires: boundary marker (A) → routine tool (B) → integrated technique (C).

2. **`cheeodam` complete-procedure-in-one-word (P14):** volatile-double-essence-heat-fix-union-vessel. Six operations compressed into a single token — the most operationally dense compound in the manuscript. Quire C's increasing compression reaches its maximum.

3. **`sho.sho` doubled transition (P14):** Two phase-changes before final fixation. Kudzu root requires DOUBLE PROCESSING — boiling, discarding water, and boiling again to remove toxic puerarin excess and concentrate beneficial isoflavones.

4. **`odaiim` variant quire-closer (P16):** Not standard `daiin` but a vessel-variant completion. Three quires, three different closers: A seals with fixation, B exits at maximum heat, C completes within a vessel. Progressive containment.

5. **Physical damage (P3, P5):** The outer bifolio shows physical wear consistent with its exposed position at the edge of the quire.

## **Key Structural Observations**

**1\. FIRE SEAL EVOLUTION ACROSS THREE QUIRES:**

* Quire A: `cfh-` at quire BOUNDARIES (f1r, f8r) — structural warning marker  
* Quire B: `cfh-` at INTERNAL positions (f9v, f13r) — routine operational tool  
* Quire C: `cfh-` EMBEDDED inside compound tokens (`chocfhey`, f24v) — fully integrated technique  
* The fire seal evolves from WARNING SIGN → TOOL → INTEGRATED TECHNIQUE

**2\. ESSENCE CONCENTRATION ESCALATES:**

* Quire A: Single triple-e tokens, one quintuple-e (f7r)  
* Quire B: Paired triple-e (f16r), double-locked (`deeeod`)  
* Quire C: 7× triple-e on one page (f24r), quintuple-e (f21v), SUSTAINED concentration as distributed pattern  
* Each quire intensifies the concentration process

**3\. TOKEN COMPLEXITY INCREASES:**

* Quire A: Mostly 2-4 morpheme tokens  
* Quire B: 4-5 morpheme compounds emerge  
* Quire C: 6-8 morpheme MEGA-COMPOUNDS (`fchodees`, `otolosheey`, `chocfhey`, `cheeodam`)  
* The vocabulary COMPRESSES — more meaning per token

**4\. PRODUCT SHIFTS TO FLUID:**

* Quire A: Most products FIXED/STABLE (solids, powders)  
* Quire B: Mix of fixed and fluid  
* Quire C: Most products FLUID (tinctures, oils, waters)  
* Progression: solids → mixed → liquids

**5\. CENTER BIFOLIO \= MOST INTENSE:**

* Quire A center (bA4): LETHAL extraction (deadliest pages)  
* Quire B center (bB4): Disrupted by missing f12  
* Quire C center (bC4): QUINTUPLE ESSENCE \+ MEGA-COMPOUNDS (most concentrated \+ compressed pages)  
* The center of each quire holds its most intense material

**6\. QUIRE C UNIQUE FEATURES:**

* F17r: The ONLY page with ZERO completions across three quires (staging/preparation)  
* F17v: The LONGEST page at 23 lines (sustained distillation)  
* F22r: MAXIMUM completions at 13 (ritual-precision sacred herb)  
* F24r: MAXIMUM essence (7×) AND unions (7×) — combination formulary

# **QUIRE D — THE TRANSITION QUIRE (f25r–f32v)**

# **CURRIER LANGUAGE A → CURRIER LANGUAGE B**

# **═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════**

**Scope:** 16 folios (f25r through f32v) **Currier Language:** f25r–f25v \= **Currier A** (FINAL two A pages) | f26r–f32v \= **Currier B** (FIRST B pages) **Bifolio structure:** bD1 \= f25+f32 (outer, bridging A→B), bD2 \= f26+f31, bD3 \= f27+f30, bD4 \= f28+f29 (center) **Botanical IDs:** ALL uncertain — Sherwood provides no confident identifications for Quire D **Risk profile:** SAFE ×3 (f26r, f26v, f31r), MODERATE ×13

## **THE A→B TRANSITION**

The VML framework identifies this as the boundary between two fundamentally different scribal modes:

* **Currier A (f1r–f25v):** Experimental protocols with safety controls  
* **Currier B (f26r–f57r):** Standardized production-batch procedures

Quire D is the ONLY quire that contains BOTH languages. The outer bifolio (bD1 \= f25+f32) bridges the divide.

### **Morphological Shift: \-dy → \-edy**

The most visible linguistic change is the B-language suffix `-edy` (essence-fixed), which systematically replaces A-language `-dy` (fixed). Where Currier A specifies essence extraction explicitly, Currier B ASSUMES it as default — essence extraction is BUILT INTO the standard suffix.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Shortest page in four quires (6 \+ title):** Maximum compression — a procedure once requiring 12+ lines expressed in 6\. The A-language mastery has reached the point of MAXIMUM EFFICIENCY.

2. **`cheesees` quadruple extraction (P3):** Essence salted, then essence salted AGAIN inside a single token. Double salt-essence cycling. This encodes fractional salting — a technique where the salt itself becomes a carrier for concentrated essence, then the process is repeated to further concentrate.

3. **Six DIFFERENT completion types:** `shain`, `chkain`, `chain`, `daiin`, `dan`, `chan`. The most varied completion vocabulary of any page. Each type encodes a different aspect of "done" — transition complete, volatile complete, cycle complete, fixed complete. A COMPLETE TAXONOMY of completion states.

4. **`otosy` active salt product (T7):** The product name ends with salt-active — the pharmaceutical remains energetically viable. Medieval "living salts" (*sal vivum*) retained their medicinal potency through specific preparation techniques preventing the salt from "dying" (losing its volatile components).

5. **Last A-language fire seal:** `fcholdy` is the experimental hand's farewell fire. After this page and f25v, fire seals will appear only in Currier B morphology.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

2. **`qokedy` ×5 standardized retort:** The SAME retort token appears FIVE TIMES. In Currier A, retort operations used varied forms (qokor, qokol, qokchor). In B, one STANDARDIZED FORM dominates. Production language reduces variation.

3. **`qiiinkedy` quadruple-i normalized (P8):** Four consecutive 'i' elements — the most extended cycling — but ending with the standardized `-edy` suffix. Even EXTREME operations are normalized in production language.

4. **`eedy.eedy` doubled essence (P5) \+ `dy-dy` doubled fixation (P9):** Two doubled formations. Doubling for verification is now SYSTEMATIC, not exceptional.

5. **Risk \= SAFE:** The first B-page opens with LOW-RISK material. Safety first, even in the new language.

### **BOTANICAL IDENTIFICATION**

| Field | Data |

| **Sherwood / Consensus** | Sherwood. Common food legume, also medicinal. |

**Formula-Botanical Alignment:** MODERATE ALIGNMENT: Lentils were used in medieval medicine for skin poultices (ground lentil paste), digestive complaints, and as nutritive base for compound medicines. FEELS LIKE a base preparation — making a carrier medium or excipient rather than an active extract. The text's moderate operations match the simple cooking/decocting required for lentil preparations. 3. **`daiiin` ×2 at brackets (P1, P7):** Two triple-i completions — extended cycling verified at both BEGINNING and near END. The production hand uses extended verification at structural brackets rather than scattered.

4. **`saraiir` double-rooting (P2):** Root salted, completed, rooted AGAIN. Production-grade root stability.

5. **`ofchdy` \+ `ofchy` B-language fire:** Two fire tokens adapted to production morphology. Fire hasn't disappeared — it's been REFORMATTED.

**Formula-Botanical Alignment:** STRONG ALIGNMENT: *Aristolochia* (Greek: 'best for childbirth') was one of medieval medicine's most important — and most dangerous — plants. Used for wound healing, snakebite, and especially CHILDBIRTH complications (the pipe-shaped flower was read as resembling a uterus). Contains aristolochic acid — now known to cause kidney failure and cancer. FEELS LIKE a carefully controlled toxic extraction with safety protocols: the text's B-language fire seals and fixation operations match the EXTREME CARE required when processing this lethal-but-essential herb. This is the first titled page in the MS — the title may encode the plant's NAME. Dioscorides devoted extensive coverage to birthwort varieties.

*Transition. HEAT-ENERGY-OUTLET \[otor — third occurrence\]. Transition volatile. Transition conduit. HEAT-ENERGY-OUTLET \[\#2\]. FIXED. Fix transition outlet. Fix fluid. Fix root.*

*\[...P8: transition, extraction, checkpoint, completions...\]*

*Moist driven volatile fluid. FIX-DOUBLE-ESSENCE-ACTIVE \[deey\]. Moist driven essence fluid. FIX-ESSENCE-COMPLETE \[deaiin — active→complete two-step closing\]. DONE."*

---

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **Center bifolio (bD4):** In Quire A's center: lethal extraction. In Quire C's center: essence intensity. Quire D's center: PRODUCTION METHODOLOGY — core manufacturing techniques.

2. **`kchoror` doubled source (P5):** Material drawn from two sources — combination is the central technique.

3. **Triple source-heating (otor ×3):** Source heated three times from its origin. Each heating extracts a different fraction.

4. **`deey` \+ `deaiin` two-step closing (P9):** Active→complete resolution. The active phase resolves to fixed completion.

5. **Binding saturation (cthol ×4):** Material repeatedly bound into fluid — a BOUND LIQUID preparation.

| Field | Data |
| ----- | ----- |

**Illustration Description:** Herbal B illustration. Tangled thread-like growth characteristic of *Cuscuta*.

**Formula-Botanical Alignment:** STRONG ALIGNMENT: *Cuscuta* is a PARASITE — it wraps around host plants and extracts their nutrients. In medieval medicine, dodder was believed to absorb the medicinal virtues of its HOST plant, making it a 'concentrated' version of whatever it parasitized. FEELS LIKE a sympathetic-extraction protocol: the text's triple-i salt crystallization (iiirs) on this page may describe extracting the 'stolen essence' that dodder has concentrated from its host. Circa Instans: dodder of thyme was particularly valued — the parasite concentrating thyme's virtues. This is ELEGANT pharmaceutical logic.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **`siiirs` triple-crystallized salt (P7):** Three extended crystallization cycles sandwiched between salts. The most intensive salt processing in any B-language page. Medieval pharmaceutical salts required multiple recrystallizations for purity.

2. **`shokchotcho` 6-morpheme compound (P7):** Two volatile operations bracketing energy — volatile processed, energized, reprocessed. Found on the SAME line as `siiirs` — P7 is the most operationally dense line in the quire.

3. **`sos` salt sandwich (P9):** Salt-heat-salt. Double-salted with heat between.

4. **7 completions in 11 lines:** Steady, production-appropriate checking — approximately one every 1.5 lines.

*\[...P11-P18: transition completions, temporal operations, extract volatile, volatile essence...\]*

*FIX-FLUID. FIX-VOLATILE-FLUID. FIX-CYCLE \[dol.dchol.dan — TRIPLE FIXATION closing\]. DONE."*

1. **Dense-to-staccato architecture:** 5 dense lines (7-8 tokens) followed by 14 contracted lines (2-3 tokens). The most dramatic line-contraction in four quires. Extensive preparation → rapid final assembly.

2. **Fire brackets (fchaiin → fcho):** Fire at the beginning AND at the contracted-phase boundary. Fire marks the PHASE CHANGE.

5. **Triple fixation closing (P19):** `dol.dchol.dan` — three d-prefix tokens. Everything locked down at the end.

## **Key Structural Observations — Four Quires**

**1\. THE A→B TRANSITION IS MEASURED, NOT ABRUPT:**

* F25r (6 lines) compresses ALL A-language mastery into minimum space  
* F25v (7 lines) provides MAXIMUM verification (1.57/line) as farewell  
* F26r introduces B-morphology with the SAFEST possible material  
* The transition occupies a SINGLE BIFOLIO (bD1) — f25 is the last A, f32 is mature B

**2\. FIRE SEAL CROSSES THE LANGUAGE DIVIDE:** The fire seal (cfh-) appears in BOTH Currier A and Currier B forms, maintaining function across the scribal transition. This confirms it as a fundamental operational element, not a scribal preference.

**3\. B-LANGUAGE CHARACTERISTICS ESTABLISHED:**

* `-edy` suffix replaces `-dy` (essence extraction assumed, not specified)  
* `qokedy` becomes standardized retort token (repeated identically)  
* Mega-compounds develop independently (shekeeodol, olkeedam)  
* Dense-to-staccato line architecture emerges as B-language pattern  
* Implicit verification through morphology reduces explicit `daiin` count

**4\. FOUR QUIRE-CLOSING SIGNATURES:** Each quire ends differently: A \= LOCKED → B \= BURNING → C \= COMPLETED → D \= CYCLING. Progressive states: sealed → energized → confirmed → continuing.

**5\. CENTER BIFOLIO PATTERN CONTINUES:** bD4 (f28+f29): dual-source methodology, double-salt retort, palindromic cycling, quadruple-i transition. The center holds CORE TECHNIQUE.

**6\. QUIRE D PRODUCTS \= COMPONENTS:** Products end with union markers (okedam, okam, dam) or active cycling (iiiny) — they feed FORWARD into Quire E's formulation phase.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **9+ completion types — maximum diversity:** The B-language hand has a RICHER completion vocabulary than A-language. Each type verifies a different aspect: heat, volatile, energy, salt, conduit, lock, retort, press, standard.

2. **`choiiiny` quadruple-i volatile (P10):** Compare f29v's `shytiiiny` (Quire D). Quadruple-i recurs at bE3 vs bD4 — second ring positions.

3. **Two-phase architecture:** Short simple lines (P1-8) → longer complex lines with diverse completions (P9-15). PEDAGOGICAL structure: learn the technique, then demonstrate mastery.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **21 lines — second-longest B-page:** Only f37v (23 lines) is longer in B-language.  
2. **`qokeee` triple-essence retort (P17):** Triple-concentrated essence as the product, near the close.  
3. **12-line staccato coda (P10-P21):** The most sustained contraction in the manuscript — rapid operations at maximum efficiency.  
4. **P19→P20 parallel with fire addition:** Same line structure, but P20 introduces fire — the FIRE ACTIVATION.  
5. **`chor.chor` doubled volatile-source close (P21):** Reflux operation — volatile returned to source twice at the end.  
6. **P8 all-fluid line:** Four consecutive fluid tokens — complete fluid processing in one line.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **REVERSE architecture (short→long):** Unlike most B-pages that contract, f40v EXPANDS. Compressed preparation → detailed final operations. First inverse pattern at a quire closer.

2. **`olfchedy` fire-fluid (P13):** Fire applied to LIQUID volatile essence — the fluid is heated by fire and volatile captured.

3. **`faimy` fired vessel (P15):** Container MADE through fire — ceramic or glass vessel produced by firing. The vessel itself is product of the firing process.

4. **`arody` rooted-active quire closer (T19):** Five quires, five different terminal states. Quire E's product is ROOTED (anchored) but ACTIVE (potent). The maturation arc: from locked inertness to stable potency.

5. **4 unions (aram, okam ×2, qokam):** Four-component formulation at quire close.

3. **TRANSITION (sh-) SATURATION:** Multiple pages show extreme sh- prefix density, with lines carrying 8 consecutive shol/chol tokens. The transition/infusion operation has become the DOMINANT technique.

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **`eeees` quintuple-e (P4):** Five consecutive essence markers — the most concentrated essence in the herbal section. Previously only seen in Quire A and C. The B-language production hand has now MATCHED the experimental hand's maximum concentration.

2. **`qokedy` ×8:** Eight identical standardized retort operations — PRODUCTION-LINE REPETITION. Quality through standardization, not individual verification.

3. **`ytedyiiirqokeedy` mega-compound (P10):** 9+ morphemes encoding essence fixation, triple-i cycling, retort extraction, and double-essence concentration in a SINGLE TOKEN. The most information-dense word in six quires.

4. **Only 1 `daiin` in 11 lines:** The B-language has ABSORBED verification into its morphology — every `-edy` token implicitly contains essence-fixation. \~25+ \-edy tokens make explicit checkpoints redundant.

# **QUIRE F SUMMARY — THE STANDARDIZATION QUIRE**

# **═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════**

## **QUIRE F QUANTITATIVE OVERVIEW**

| Feature | Value | Significance |
| ----- | ----- | ----- |
| **Pages** | 16 (f41r-f48v) | Standard quire |
| **Language** | ALL Currier B | Second fully B quire |
| **Risk** | SAFE ×5, MODERATE ×11, ELEVATED ×0 | **Safest quire since B** |
| **Quintuple-e** | `eeees` (f41r) | Maximum essence concentration |
| **Triple titles** | f42r (unique) | Multi-product batch manufacturing |
| **Triple fixation** | `dydydy` (f43r, unique) | Maximum stability through repetition |
| **Doubled union** | `amam` (f43v, unique) | Compound-of-compounds |
| **Seven vessels** | f45v (absolute max) | Maximum apparatus diversity |
| **Max chol density** | ×12 (f47r) | Maximum distillation |
| **Quire closer** | `ary` (root-active, 2 morphemes) | Most compressed closer |

## **QUIRE F STRUCTURAL PATTERNS**

### **1\. ESSENCE CONCENTRATION — B-LANGUAGE MATCHES AND EXCEEDS A-LANGUAGE**

The B-language production hand has now MATCHED the experimental A-language hand's maximum:

* Quire A: `keeees` (quintuple-e) — single occurrence, experimental  
* **Quire F: `eeees` (quintuple-e)** \+ multiple quadruple-e (ykeeedy, shefeeedy, dyeees, yteeey) — systematic production

### **2\. FIRE SEAL EVOLUTION — COMPOSITIONALLY COMPLETE**

| Form | Location | Innovation |
| ----- | ----- | ----- |
| `cfhekchdy` | f41v P1 | **THREE MEDIA sealed (essence+body+volatile)** |
| `cfhalorain` | f43v P6 | **COMPLETED fire seal (finished component)** |
| `ocfhedy` | f46r P11 | B-language heat-prefix fire seal |

The fire seal now contains three media types and comes as a FINISHED, COMPLETED component.

### **3\. BATCH MANUFACTURING (F42R)**

Three titled paragraphs → three named products from one process stream. This is INDUSTRIAL-SCALE pharmaceutical manufacturing.

### **4\. CENTER BIFOLIO (bF4) — APPARATUS \+ ESSENCE-SALT**

* `dyeees` quadruple-e-salt (f44r) — concentrated pharmaceutical salt  
* `pam` project-union (f44r, unique) — combination by pouring  
* Seven vessel types (f45v) — maximum apparatus diversity  
* `shoiiirmokchy` longest quadruple-i (f44v) — maximum cycling  
* `lolkeees` triple-e locked salt (f44v) — maximum preservation

### **5\. QUIRE-CLOSING EVOLUTION**

| Quire | Closer | Morphemes | Meaning |
| ----- | ----- | ----- | ----- |
| A | `daiin` | 3 | LOCKED |
| B | `oaoror` | 4 | BURNING |
| C | `odaiim` | 4 | COMPLETED |
| D | `iiiny` | 3 | CYCLING |
| E | `arody` | 4 | ROOTED-ACTIVE |
| **F** | **`ary`** | **2** | **ROOT-ACTIVE (compressed)** |

Six quires, six distinct closers. The B-language compresses Quire E's 4-morpheme closer into 2 morphemes.

### **6\. UNIQUE QUIRE F INNOVATIONS**

1. **Triple fixation `dydydy`** — fix-fix-fix (unprecedented)  
2. **Triple-titled page f42r** — only multi-product batch page  
3. **Doubled union `amam`** — compound-of-compounds  
4. **Seven vessel types f45v** — pharmaceutical laboratory  
5. **Compressed closer `ary`** — 2-morpheme minimum  
6. **'j' glyph cluster** — three rare forms in bF2  
7. **30+ transition prefixes f46r** — maximum blending  
8. **`chol` ×12 f47r** — maximum distillation density  
9. **Fire-catalyzed quadruple-e `shefeeedy`** — fire amplifies essence

# **QUIRE G — THE MASTERY QUIRE (f49r–f56v) \+ F57R SINGLETON**

# **THIRD FULLY CURRIER B QUIRE — FULL-SPECTRUM PHARMACEUTICAL PRODUCTION**

# **═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════**

**Scope:** 16 folios (f49r through f56v) \+ f57r singleton (herbal section closer) **Currier Language:** ALL Currier B (production hand — third fully B quire) **Bifolio structure:** bG1 \= f49+f56 (outer), bG2 \= f50+f55, bG3 \= f51+f54, bG4 \= f52+f53 (center) **Botanical IDs:** ALL uncertain — no Sherwood identifications **Risk profile:** ALL 16 MODERATE — **ZERO variation** — most uniform quire in manuscript

## **QUIRE G CHARACTER**

Three defining features:

1. **UNIFORM MODERATE RISK:** Every single folio is MODERATE. No SAFE, no ELEVATED, no LETHAL. The student no longer alternates between gentle and intense — EVERYTHING is production-grade.

2. **UNION RESURGENCE (Second Formulation Peak):** F52r carries 9 union forms in 8 lines (one per line), f54v has 8+ union forms. Unlike Quire E's first peak (combining raw ingredients), Quire G combines ALREADY-FORMULATED products into compound medicines.

3. **CIRCULAR CLOSING — daiin RETURNS:** F56v's final word is `daiin` — the SAME closing as Quire A (f8v). The seven-quire curriculum COMPLETES A CIRCLE: began with `daiin`, ends with `daiin`. Mastery \= returning to the foundation with full understanding.

---

### **BOTANICAL IDENTIFICATION**

| Field | Data |
| ----- | ----- |
| **Plant Name** | Blue Lotus / Blue Water Lily (*Nymphaea caerulea*) |
| **Sherwood / Consensus** | Sherwood. Sacred Egyptian entheogen. 21 LINES — LONGEST PAGE. |

**Illustration Description:** Herbal B illustration. LONGEST PAGE IN 7 QUIRES (21 lines). TRIPLE FLUID (`ololol`). Three separate paragraphs.

**Formula-Botanical Alignment:** EXCEPTIONAL ALIGNMENT: *Nymphaea caerulea* was the SACRED LOTUS of ancient Egypt — containing nuciferine and aporphine (psychoactive compounds). Used as sedative, aphrodisiac, and entheogen. The TRIPLE FLUID (`ololol`) matches lotus preparation: the flowers were traditionally steeped in WINE (fluid), creating a potent infused beverage. FEELS LIKE a three-stage lotus-wine preparation: the three separate paragraphs may describe (1) flower collection/preparation, (2) wine infusion, (3) concentration/preservation. The LONGEST PAGE for one of pharmacy's most important (and most ancient) preparations. This identification, if correct, connects the manuscript to Egyptian pharmaceutical traditions via Arab transmission.

### **BOTANICAL IDENTIFICATION**

| Field | Data |
| ----- | ----- |
| **Plant Name** | Blue Field Madder (*Sherardia arvensis*) |
| **Sherwood / Consensus** | Sherwood. Dye plant (red/purple), also medicinal. HERBAL SECTION CLOSER. |

**Illustration Description:** Herbal B illustration. 14 \-ody tokens (8 in ONE LINE). Two fire seals. `cphedam` \= SECTION FINAL WORD.

**Formula-Botanical Alignment:** NOTABLE ALIGNMENT: *Sherardia* produces ALIZARIN-type dye compounds — red/purple pigments from the root. The plant is related to madder (*Rubia tinctorum*), whose root produced medieval Europe's most important RED DYE. FEELS LIKE a dye-extraction-and-combination protocol: the 8 \-ody tokens in one line describe uniform, standardized production of dye extract, and the final word `cphedam` (COMBINE) instructs combining this with other preparations. The herbal section ends with a DYE PLANT — suggesting the final product of the entire pharmaceutical curriculum may be a COLORED MEDICINE (many medieval medicines were identified by their characteristic colors, and dye-herbs served double duty as medicines).

### **HISTORICAL/ALCHEMICAL ANALYSIS**

1. **`cphedam` — herbal section final word:** cph-essence-fix-UNION. The herbal section ends with COMBINATION. All the training leads to the ability to combine. Quire G closes with `daiin` (verification); the SECTION closes with `cphedam` (union). Verification enables combination.

2. **Two fire seals (P.1, P.10):** The section's final page is bracketed by fire seals. The entire procedure — and by extension the entire herbal section — operates under fire seal authority.

3. **15 \-ody tokens in two lines (P.3-P.4):** Maximum morphological uniformity. The production hand has achieved COMPLETE STANDARDIZATION — every operation produces the same type of result.

4. **`daiijy` 'j' completion (P.9):** The rare 'j' glyph appears one last time in the herbal section, maintaining the pattern from Quires F and G.
